dollar">Pitcairn Islands dollar</a> is treated as a collectible/souvenir currency outside Pitcairn (<a href="/wiki/Non-circulating_legal_tender" title="Non-circulating legal tender">non-circulating legal tender</a>). <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">U.S. dollar</a> also widely accepted due to cruise ships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">Pound sterling</a> also accepted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></li>\n</ol></div></td></tr><tr style="font-size:90%;"><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><div style="text-align:left;margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;"><b><a href="/wiki/Postcodes_in_the_United_Kingdom#British_Overseas_Territories" title="Postcodes in the United Kingdom">UK Postcode</a></b><span class="nowrap">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span>PCRN 1ZZ</div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Pitcairn Islands</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'p\' in \'pie\'">p</span><span title="/&#618;/: \'i\' in \'kit\'">&#618;</span><span title="\'t\' in \'tie\'">t</span><span title="\'k\' in \'kind\'">k</span><span title="/&#603;&#601;r/: \'are\' in \'bare\'">&#603;&#601;r</span><span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitkern" title="Pitkern">Pitkern</a>: <i><i lang="pih" title="Pitcairn-Norfolk language text">Pitkern Ailen</i></i>), officially <b>Pitcairn, Henderson, Ducie and Oeno Islands</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BNA1981_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-BNA1981-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Order2010_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Order2010-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PitcainLaws_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-PitcainLaws-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TheOverTerr_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-TheOverTerr-11">[11]</a></sup> are a group of four <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcanic</a> islands in the southern <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a> that form the sole <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territory</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Pacific_Ocean" title="South Pacific Ocean">South Pacific</a>. The four islands&#160;&#8211; Pitcairn proper, <a href="/wiki/Henderson_Island_(Pitcairn_Islands)" title="Henderson Island (Pitcairn Islands)">Henderson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ducie_Island" title="Ducie Island">Ducie</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Oeno_Island" title="Oeno Island">Oeno</a>&#160;&#8211; are scattered across several hundred miles of ocean and have a combined land area of about 47 square kilometres (18&#160;sq&#160;mi). Henderson Island accounts for 86% of the land area, but only Pitcairn Island is inhabited. The nearest places are <a href="/wiki/Mangareva" title="Mangareva">Mangareva</a> (of <a href="/wiki/French_Polynesia" title="French Polynesia">French Polynesia</a>) to the west and <a href="/wiki/Easter_Island" title="Easter Island">Easter Island</a> to the east.\n</p><p>Pitcairn is the least populous national jurisdiction in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Pitcairn_Islanders" title="Pitcairn Islanders">Pitcairn Islanders</a> are a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biracial" title="Biracial">biracial</a> ethnic group descended mostly from nine <a href="/wiki/Mutiny_on_the_Bounty" title="Mutiny on the Bounty"><i>Bounty</i> mutineers</a> and the handful of <a href="/wiki/Tahitians" title="Tahitians">Tahitians</a> who accompanied them, an event that has been retold in many books and films. This history is still apparent in the surnames of many of the islanders. Today there are approximately 50 permanent inhabitants, originating from four main families.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-government.pn_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-government.pn-13">[13]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-41"><a href="#Government"><span class="tocnumber">15.1</span> <span class="toctext">Government</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-42"><a href="#Travel"><span class="tocnumber">15.2</span> <span class="toctext">Travel</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-43"><a href="#Local_news"><span class="tocnumber">15.3</span> <span class="toctext">Local news</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-44"><a href="#Study_groups"><span class="tocnumber">15.4</span> <span class="toctext">Study groups</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Pitcairn_Islands" title="History of the Pitcairn Islands">History of the Pitcairn Islands</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pitcairn_Island_In_The_Distance.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Pitcairn_Island_In_The_Distance.jpg/220px-Pitcairn_Island_In_The_Distance.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Pitcairn_Island_In_The_Distance.jpg/330px-Pitcairn_Island_In_The_Distance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Pitcairn_Island_In_The_Distance.jpg/440px-Pitcairn_Island_In_The_Distance.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pitcairn_Island_In_The_Distance.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>West side of Pitcairn Island</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pitcairnlanding.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Pitcairnlanding.jpg/220px-Pitcairnlanding.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Pitcairnlanding.jpg/330px-Pitcairnlanding.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Pitcairnlanding.jpg/440px-Pitcairnlanding.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pitcairnlanding.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pitcairn Landing</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Adamstown1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="985" data-file-width="1431" decoding="async" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Adamstown1.jpg/220px-Adamstown1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Adamstown1.jpg/330px-Adamstown1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Adamstown1.jpg/440px-Adamstown1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Adamstown1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Adamstown, the only settlement in the islands</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Polynesian_settlement_and_extinction">Polynesian settlement and extinction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Polynesian settlement and extinction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The earliest known settlers of the Pitcairn Islands were <a href="/wiki/Polynesians" title="Polynesians">Polynesians</a> who appear to have lived on Pitcairn and Henderson, and on <a href="/wiki/Mangareva" title="Mangareva">Mangareva</a> Island 540 kilometres (340&#160;mi) to the northwest, for several centuries. They traded goods and formed social ties among the three islands despite the long canoe voyages between them, which helped the small populations on each island survive despite their limited resources. Eventually, important natural resources were exhausted, inter-island trade broke down and a period of civil war began on Mangareva, causing the small human populations on Henderson and Pitcairn to be cut off and eventually become extinct.\n</p><p>Although archaeologists believe that Polynesians were living on Pitcairn as late as the 15th century,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> the islands were uninhabited when they were rediscovered by Europeans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_discovery">European discovery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: European discovery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Ducie and Henderson Islands were discovered by Portuguese sailor <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Fernandes_de_Queir%C3%B3s" title="Pedro Fernandes de Queir&#243;s">Pedro Fernandes de Queir&#243;s</a>, sailing for the Spanish Crown, who arrived on 26&#160;January 1606. He named them La&#160;Encarnaci&#243;n ("<a href="/wiki/Incarnation_(Christianity)" title="Incarnation (Christianity)">The Incarnation</a>") and San Juan Bautista ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_John_the_Baptist" title="Saint John the Baptist">Saint John the Baptist</a>"), respectively. However, some sources express doubt about exactly which of the islands were visited and named by Queir&#243;s, suggesting that La&#160;Encarnaci&#243;n may actually have been Henderson Island, and San Juan Bautista may have been Pitcairn Island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Pitcairn Island was sighted on 3&#160;July 1767 by the crew of the British <a href="/wiki/Sloop-of-war" title="Sloop-of-war">sloop</a> <a href="/wiki/HMS_Swallow_(1732)" title="HMS Swallow (1732)">HMS <i>Swallow</i></a>, commanded by Captain <a href="/wiki/Philip_Carteret" title="Philip Carteret">Philip Carteret</a>. The island was named after Midshipman <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_Pitcairn_(midshipman)" title="Robert Pitcairn (midshipman)">Robert Pitcairn</a>, a fifteen-year-old crew member who was the first to sight the island. Robert Pitcairn was a son of British Marine Major <a href="/wiki/John_Pitcairn" title="John Pitcairn">John Pitcairn</a>, who later was killed at the 1775 <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bunker_Hill" title="Battle of Bunker Hill">Battle of Bunker Hill</a> in the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>.\n</p><p>Carteret, who sailed without the newly-invented <a href="/wiki/Marine_chronometer" title="Marine chronometer">marine chronometer</a>, charted the island at <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;params=25_02_S_133_21_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">25&#176;02&#8242;S</span> <span class="longitude">133&#176;21&#8242;W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#65279; / &#65279;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">25.033&#176;S 133.350&#176;W</span><span style="display:none">&#65279; / <span class="geo">-25.033; -133.350</span></span></span></a></span>, and although the <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitude</a> was reasonably accurate, his recorded <a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">longitude</a> was incorrect by about 3&#176;&#160;(330&#160;km, 210&#160;mi) west of the island. This made Pitcairn difficult to find, as highlighted by the failure of Captain <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> to locate the island in July&#160;1773.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_settlement">European settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: European settlement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mutiny_HMS_Bounty.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="931" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Mutiny_HMS_Bounty.jpg/220px-Mutiny_HMS_Bounty.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Mutiny_HMS_Bounty.jpg/330px-Mutiny_HMS_Bounty.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Mutiny_HMS_Bounty.jpg/440px-Mutiny_HMS_Bounty.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mutiny_HMS_Bounty.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The mutineers turning Bligh and part of the officers and crew adrift from the <a href="/wiki/HMS_Bounty" title="HMS Bounty"><i>Bounty</i></a>, 29 April 1789</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/HMS_Bounty" title="HMS Bounty">HMS Bounty</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mutiny_on_the_Bounty" title="Mutiny on the Bounty">Mutiny on the Bounty</a></div>\n<p>In 1790 nine of the mutineers from the <i>Bounty</i>, along with the native <a href="/wiki/Tahiti" title="Tahiti">Tahitian</a> men and women who were with them (six men, eleven women, and a baby girl), settled on Pitcairn Islands and set fire to the <i>Bounty</i>. The wreck is still visible underwater in <a href="/wiki/Bounty_Bay" title="Bounty Bay">Bounty Bay</a>, discovered in 1957 by <i><a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Society" title="National Geographic Society">National Geographic</a></i> explorer <a href="/wiki/Luis_Marden" title="Luis Marden">Luis Marden</a>. Although the settlers survived by farming and fishing, the initial period of settlement was marked by serious tensions among them. <a href="/wiki/Alcoholism" title="Alcoholism">Alcoholism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Murder" title="Murder">murder</a>, disease, and other ills took the lives of most mutineers and Tahitian men. <a href="/wiki/John_Adams_(mutineer)" title="John Adams (mutineer)">John Adams</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ned_Young" title="Ned Young">Ned Young</a> turned to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scriptures" title="Scriptures">scriptures</a>, using the ship\'s <a href="/wiki/Bounty_Bible" title="Bounty Bible">Bible</a> as their guide for a new and peaceful society. Young eventually died of an <a href="/wiki/Asthma" title="Asthma">asthmatic</a> infection.\n</p><p>Ducie Island was rediscovered in 1791 by Royal Navy Captain Edwards aboard <a href="/wiki/HMS_Pandora_(1779)" title="HMS Pandora (1779)">HMS <i>Pandora</i></a>, while searching for the Bounty mutineers. He named it after <a href="/wiki/Francis_Reynolds-Moreton,_3rd_Baron_Ducie" title="Francis Reynolds-Moreton, 3rd Baron Ducie">Francis Reynolds-Moreton, 3rd&#160;Baron Ducie</a>, also a captain in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Royal_Navy" title="British Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>.\n</p><p>The Pitcairn islanders reported it was not until 27&#160;December 1795 that the first ship since the <i>Bounty</i> was seen from the island, but it did not approach the land and they could not make out the nationality. A second ship appeared in 1801, but made no attempt to communicate with them. A third came sufficiently near to see their house, but did not try to send a boat on shore. Finally, the American <a href="/wiki/Seal_hunting" title="Seal hunting">sealing</a> ship <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Topaz_(ship)" title="Topaz (ship)">Topaz</a></i> under <a href="/wiki/Mayhew_Folger" title="Mayhew Folger">Mayhew Folger</a> became the first to visit the island, when the crew spent 10&#160;hours on Pitcairn in February&#160;1808.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_view_of_Pitcairn%27s_Island,_South_Seas,_1814,_J._Shillibeer.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="790" data-file-width="1400" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/A_view_of_Pitcairn%27s_Island%2C_South_Seas%2C_1814%2C_J._Shillibeer.jpg/220px-A_view_of_Pitcairn%27s_Island%2C_South_Seas%2C_1814%2C_J._Shillibeer.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/A_view_of_Pitcairn%27s_Island%2C_South_Seas%2C_1814%2C_J._Shillibeer.jpg/330px-A_view_of_Pitcairn%27s_Island%2C_South_Seas%2C_1814%2C_J._Shillibeer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/A_view_of_Pitcairn%27s_Island%2C_South_Seas%2C_1814%2C_J._Shillibeer.jpg/440px-A_view_of_Pitcairn%27s_Island%2C_South_Seas%2C_1814%2C_J._Shillibeer.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_view_of_Pitcairn%27s_Island,_South_Seas,_1814,_J._Shillibeer.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view of Pitcairn\'s Island, South Seas, 1814, J. Shillibeer</div></div></div><p>A report of Folger\'s discovery was forwarded to the <a href="/wiki/Admiralty" title="Admiralty">Admiralty</a>, mentioning the mutineers and giving a more precise location of the island: <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;params=25_02_S_130_00_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">25&#176;02&#8242;S</span> <span class="longitude">130&#176;00&#8242;W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#65279; / &#65279;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">25.033&#176;S 130.000&#176;W</span><span style="display:none">&#65279; / <span class="geo">-25.033; -130.000</span></span></span></a></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> However this was not known to Sir&#160;<a href="/wiki/Thomas_Staines" title="Thomas Staines">Thomas Staines</a>, who commanded a Royal Navy <a href="/wiki/Flotilla" title="Flotilla">flotilla</a> of two ships (HMS&#160;<i>Briton</i> and HMS&#160;<i>Tagus</i>) which found the island at <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;params=25_04_S_130_25_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">25&#176;04&#8242;S</span> <span class="longitude">130&#176;25&#8242;W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#65279; / &#65279;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">25.067&#176;S 130.417&#176;W</span><span style="display:none">&#65279; / <span class="geo">-25.067; -130.417</span></span></span></a></span> (by meridian observation) on 17&#160;September 1814. Staines sent a party ashore and wrote a detailed report for the Admiralty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hist_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-hist-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> By that time, only one mutineer, John Adams, remained alive. He was granted <a href="/wiki/Amnesty" title="Amnesty">amnesty</a> for his part in the <a href="/wiki/Mutiny" title="Mutiny">mutiny</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hist_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-hist-19">[19]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Henderson Island was rediscovered on 17&#160;January 1819 by British Captain James Henderson of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_East_India_Company" title="British East India Company">British East India Company</a> ship <i>Hercules</i>. Captain Henry King, sailing on the <i>Elizabeth</i>, landed on 2&#160;March to find the king\'s colours already flying. His crew scratched the name of their ship into a tree. Oeno Island was discovered on 26&#160;January 1824 by American Captain George Worth aboard <a href="/wiki/Oeno_(ship)" title="Oeno (ship)">the whaler <i>Oeno</i></a>.\n</p><p>In 1832 a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Church_Missionary_Society" title="Church Missionary Society">Church Missionary Society</a> missionary, <a href="/wiki/Joshua_Hill_(Pitcairn_Island_leader)" title="Joshua Hill (Pitcairn Island leader)">Joshua Hill</a>, arrived; he reported that by March&#160;1833 he had founded a Temperance Society to combat drunkenness, a &#8220;Maundy Thursday Society&#8221;, a monthly prayer meeting, a juvenile society, a Peace Society, and a school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_colony">British colony</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: British colony">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/British_Western_Pacific_Territories" title="British Western Pacific Territories">British Western Pacific Territories</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pitcairn_1940_07.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="626" data-file-width="942" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Pitcairn_1940_07.jpg/200px-Pitcairn_1940_07.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Pitcairn_1940_07.jpg/300px-Pitcairn_1940_07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Pitcairn_1940_07.jpg/400px-Pitcairn_1940_07.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pitcairn_1940_07.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stamp of the Pitcairn Islands</div></div></div>\n<p>Traditionally, Pitcairn Islanders consider that their islands "officially" became a British colony on 30 November 1838, at the same time becoming <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_women%27s_suffrage" title="Timeline of women\'s suffrage">one of the first territories to extend voting rights to women</a>. By the mid-1850s, the Pitcairn community was outgrowing the island; its leaders appealed to the British government for assistance, and were offered <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Island" title="Norfolk Island">Norfolk Island</a>. On 3 May 1856, the entire population of 193 people set sail for Norfolk on board the <i>Morayshire</i>, arriving on 8 June after a difficult five-week trip. However, just eighteen months later, seventeen of the Pitcairn Islanders returned to their home island, and another 27 followed five years later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hist_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-hist-19">[19]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/HMS_Thetis_(1871)" title="HMS Thetis (1871)">HMS <i>Thetis</i></a> visited Pitcairn Island on 18 April 1881 and "found the people very happy and contented, and in perfect health". At that time the population was 96; an increase of six since the visit of <a href="/wiki/Algernon_Frederick_Rous_de_Horsey" title="Algernon Frederick Rous de Horsey">Admiral de Horsey</a> in September 1878. Stores had recently been delivered from friends in England, including two whale-boats and <a href="/wiki/Portland_cement" title="Portland cement">Portland cement</a>, which was used to make the reservoir watertight. HMS <i>Thetis</i> gave the islanders 200&#160;lb (91&#160;kg) of biscuits, 100&#160;lb (45&#160;kg) of candles, and 100&#160;lb (45&#160;kg) of soap and clothing to the value of &#163;31, donated by the <a href="/wiki/Ship%27s_company" title="Ship\'s company">ship\'s company</a>. An American trading ship called <i>Venus</i> had recently bestowed a supply of <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton seed</a>, to provide the islanders with a crop for future trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pitcairn_Islanders,_1916.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="443" data-file-width="713" decoding="async" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Pitcairn_Islanders%2C_1916.jpg/220px-Pitcairn_Islanders%2C_1916.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Pitcairn_Islanders%2C_1916.jpg/330px-Pitcairn_Islanders%2C_1916.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Pitcairn_Islanders%2C_1916.jpg/440px-Pitcairn_Islanders%2C_1916.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pitcairn_Islanders,_1916.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pitcairn Islanders, 1916</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1886, the <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist</a> layman <a href="/wiki/John_Tay" title="John Tay">John Tay</a> visited Pitcairn and persuaded most of the islanders to accept his faith. He returned in 1890 on the missionary schooner <i><a href="/wiki/Pitcairn_(schooner)" title="Pitcairn (schooner)">Pitcairn</a></i> with an ordained minister to perform baptisms. Since then, the majority of Pitcairn Islanders have been Adventists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The islands of Henderson, Oeno and Ducie were annexed by Britain in 1902: Henderson on 1 July, Oeno on 10 July, and Ducie on 19 December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> In 1938, the three islands, along with Pitcairn, were incorporated into a single administrative unit called the "Pitcairn Group of Islands".\n</p><p>The population peaked at 233 in 1937;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> it has since reduced owing to emigration, primarily to <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-2">[2]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sexual_assault_trials_of_2004">Sexual assault trials of 2004</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Sexual assault trials of 2004">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pitcairn_sexual_assault_trial_of_2004" title="Pitcairn sexual assault trial of 2004">Pitcairn sexual assault trial of 2004</a></div>\n<p>In 2004, charges were laid against seven men living on Pitcairn and six living abroad. This accounted for nearly a third of the male population. After extensive trials, most of the men were convicted, some with multiple counts of sexual encounters with children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tweedie_2004_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tweedie_2004-28">[28]</a></sup> On 25 October 2004, six men were convicted, including <a href="/wiki/Steve_Christian" title="Steve Christian">Steve Christian</a>, the island\'s mayor at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fickling_2004_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fickling_2004-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> In 2004, the islanders had about 20 guns among them, which they surrendered ahead of the <a href="/wiki/Pitcairn_sexual_assault_trial_of_2004" title="Pitcairn sexual assault trial of 2004">sexual assault trials</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> After the six men lost their final appeal, the British government set up a prison on the island at Bob\'s Valley.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The men began serving their sentences in late 2006. By 2010, all had served their sentences or been granted home detention status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010_and_2016_trials">2010 and 2016 trials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2010 and 2016 trials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2010, the mayor <a href="/wiki/Mike_Warren_(mayor)" title="Mike Warren (mayor)">Mike Warren</a> faced 25 charges of possessing images and videos of child pornography on his computer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gay_2013_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gay_2013-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> In 2016 Warren was found guilty of downloading more than 1000 images and videos of child sexual abuse. Warren began downloading the images some time after the 2004 sexual assault convictions. During the time he downloaded the images he was working in child protection. Warren was also convicted of engaging in a "sex chat" with someone who he believed was a 15-year-old girl.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_Pitcairn_Islands" title="Geography of the Pitcairn Islands">Geography of the Pitcairn Islands</a></div>\n<p>The Pitcairn Islands form the southeasternmost extension of the geological <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Tuamotus" title="Tuamotus">Tuamotus</a> of <a href="/wiki/French_Polynesia" title="French Polynesia">French Polynesia</a>, and consist of four islands: Pitcairn Island, <a href="/wiki/Oeno_Island" title="Oeno Island">Oeno Island</a> (atoll with five islets, one of which is Sandy Island), <a href="/wiki/Henderson_Island_(Pitcairn_Islands)" title="Henderson Island (Pitcairn Islands)">Henderson Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ducie_Island" title="Ducie Island">Ducie Island</a> (atoll with four islets).\n</p><p>The Pitcairn Islands were formed by a centre of upwelling <a href="/wiki/Magma" title="Magma">magma</a> called the <a href="/wiki/Pitcairn_hotspot" title="Pitcairn hotspot">Pitcairn hotspot</a>.\n</p><p>The only permanently inhabited island, Pitcairn, is accessible only by boat through Bounty Bay. Henderson Island, covering about 86% of the territory\'s total land area and supporting a rich variety of animals in its nearly inaccessible interior, is also capable of supporting a small human population despite its scarce fresh water, but access is difficult, owing to its outer shores being steep limestone cliffs covered by sharp coral. In 1988, this island was designated as a UNESCO World Heritage site.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-39">[39]</a></sup> The other islands are at a distance of more than 100&#160;km (62&#160;mi) and are not habitable.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Island or atoll</th>\n<th>Type</th>\n<th>Land
