Pitcairn Island\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 122px"><div style="width: 122px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 120px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pitcairnsatellite.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="540" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Pitcairnsatellite.png/180px-Pitcairnsatellite.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Pitcairnsatellite.png/270px-Pitcairnsatellite.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Pitcairnsatellite.png/360px-Pitcairnsatellite.png 2x" width="120"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Satellite photo of Pitcairn Island\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 123.33333333333px"><div style="width: 123.33333333333px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 121.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pitcairn_Island_Group.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="495" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Pitcairn_Island_Group.svg/182px-Pitcairn_Island_Group.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Pitcairn_Island_Group.svg/273px-Pitcairn_Island_Group.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Pitcairn_Island_Group.svg/364px-Pitcairn_Island_Group.svg.png 2x" width="122"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Map of Pitcairn Islands\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 178px"><div style="width: 178px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 176px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bounty_bay.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1500" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Bounty_bay.jpg/264px-Bounty_bay.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Bounty_bay.jpg/396px-Bounty_bay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Bounty_bay.jpg/528px-Bounty_bay.jpg 2x" width="176"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>View of <a href="/wiki/Bounty_Bay" title="Bounty Bay">Bounty Bay</a>\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Geodesy_Collection_Pitcairn_Island.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="972" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="209" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Geodesy_Collection_Pitcairn_Island.jpg/220px-Geodesy_Collection_Pitcairn_Island.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Geodesy_Collection_Pitcairn_Island.jpg/330px-Geodesy_Collection_Pitcairn_Island.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Geodesy_Collection_Pitcairn_Island.jpg/440px-Geodesy_Collection_Pitcairn_Island.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Geodesy_Collection_Pitcairn_Island.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Geodesy" title="Geodesy">Geodesy</a> operations on Pitcairn Island</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_of_the_Pitcairn_Islands" title="Climate of the Pitcairn Islands">Climate of the Pitcairn Islands</a></div>\n<p>Pitcairn is located just south of the Tropic of Capricorn and experiences year-round warm weather, with wet summers and drier winters. The rainy season (summer) is from November through to March, when temperatures average 25 to 35&#160;&#176;C (77 to 95&#160;&#176;F) and humidity can exceed 95%. Temperatures in the winter range from 17 to 25&#160;&#176;C (63 to 77&#160;&#176;F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-2">[2]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora">Flora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Flora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>About nine plant species are thought to <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">occur only</a> on Pitcairn. These include tapau, formerly an important timber resource, and the <a href="/wiki/Angiopteris" title="Angiopteris">giant nehe fern</a>. Some, such as red berry (<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Coprosma_rapensis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Coprosma rapensis (page does not exist)">Coprosma rapensis</a></i> var. <i>Benefica</i>), are perilously close to extinction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> The plant species <i><a href="/wiki/Glochidion_pitcairnense" title="Glochidion pitcairnense">Glochidion pitcairnense</a></i> is endemic to Pitcairn and Henderson Islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna">Fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_the_Pitcairn_Islands" title="List of birds of the Pitcairn Islands">List of birds of the Pitcairn Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_Pitcairn" title="List of mammals of Pitcairn">List of mammals of Pitcairn</a></div>\n<p>Between 1937 and 1951, <a href="/wiki/Irving_Johnson" title="Irving Johnson">Irving Johnson</a>, skipper of the 29-metre (96&#160;ft) brigantine <i>Yankee Five</i>, introduced five <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_giant_tortoise" title="Gal&#225;pagos giant tortoise">Gal&#225;pagos giant tortoises</a> to Pitcairn. <a href="/wiki/Mr_Turpen" title="Mr Turpen">Turpen</a>, also known as Mr. Turpen or Mr. T, is the sole survivor. Turpen usually lives at Tedside by Western Harbour. A protection order makes it an offence should anyone kill, injure, capture, maim, or cause harm or distress to the tortoise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The birds of Pitcairn fall into several groups. These include seabirds, wading birds and a small number of resident land-bird species. Of 20 breeding species, Henderson Island has 16, including the unique flightless <a href="/wiki/Henderson_crake" title="Henderson crake">Henderson crake</a>; Oeno hosts 12; Ducie 13 and Pitcairn six species. Birds breeding on Pitcairn include the <a href="/wiki/Fairy_tern" title="Fairy tern">fairy tern</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Common_noddy" title="Common noddy">common noddy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Red-tailed_tropicbird" title="Red-tailed tropicbird">red-tailed tropicbird</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Pitcairn_reed_warbler" title="Pitcairn reed warbler">Pitcairn reed warbler</a>, known by Pitcairners as a "sparrow", is endemic to Pitcairn Island; formerly common, it was added to the <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">endangered species</a> list in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A small population of <a href="/wiki/Humpback_whale" title="Humpback whale">humpback whales</a> which has been poorly studied annually migrate to the islands to winter and breed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Important_bird_areas">Important bird areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Important bird areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The four islands in the Pitcairn group have been identified by <a href="/wiki/BirdLife_International" title="BirdLife International">BirdLife International</a> as separate <a href="/wiki/Important_Bird_Area" title="Important Bird Area">Important Bird Areas</a> (IBAs). Pitcairn Island is recognised because it is the only nesting site of the <a href="/wiki/Pitcairn_reed_warbler" title="Pitcairn reed warbler">Pitcairn reed warbler</a>. Henderson Island is important for its endemic land-birds as well as its breeding <a href="/wiki/Seabird" title="Seabird">seabirds</a>. Oeno\'s ornithological significance derives principally from its <a href="/wiki/Murphy%27s_petrel" title="Murphy\'s petrel">Murphy\'s petrel</a> colony. Ducie is important for its colonies of <a href="/wiki/Murphy%27s_petrel" title="Murphy\'s petrel">Murphy\'s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herald_petrel" title="Herald petrel">herald</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kermadec_petrel" title="Kermadec petrel">Kermadec petrels</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Christmas_shearwater" title="Christmas shearwater">Christmas shearwaters</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pitcairn_Islands_Marine_Reserve">Pitcairn Islands Marine Reserve</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Pitcairn Islands Marine Reserve">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In March 2015 the British government established <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_protected_areas" title="List of largest protected areas">one of the largest</a> <a href="/wiki/Marine_protected_area" title="Marine protected area">marine protected areas</a> in the world around the Pitcairn Islands. The reserve covers the islands\' entire <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zone" title="Exclusive economic zone">exclusive economic zone</a>&#160;&#8211; 834,334 square kilometres (322,138&#160;sq&#160;mi). The intention is to protect some of the world\'s most pristine ocean habitat from illegal fishing activities. A satellite "watchroom" dubbed Project Eyes on the Seas has been established by the <a href="/wiki/UK_Space_Agency" title="UK Space Agency">Satellite Applications Catapult</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Pew_Charitable_Trusts" title="The Pew Charitable Trusts">the Pew Charitable Trusts</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Harwell_Science_and_Innovation_Campus" title="Harwell Science and Innovation Campus">Harwell Science and Innovation Campus</a> in <a href="/wiki/Harwell,_Oxfordshire" title="Harwell, Oxfordshire">Harwell, Oxfordshire</a> to monitor vessel activity and to gather the information needed to prosecute unauthorised trawling.\n<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gauke_2015_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gauke_2015-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Pitcairn_Islands" title="Politics of the Pitcairn Islands">Politics of the Pitcairn Islands</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1358" data-file-width="2206" decoding="async" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/220px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/330px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/440px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the European Union in the world with overseas countries and territories and outermost regions</div></div></div>\n<p>The Pitcairn Islands are a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_overseas_territory" title="British overseas territory">British overseas territory</a> with a degree of local government. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Queen of the United Kingdom">Queen of the United Kingdom</a> is represented by a Governor, who also holds office as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_High_Commissioners_of_the_United_Kingdom_to_New_Zealand" title="List of High Commissioners of the United Kingdom to New Zealand">British High Commissioner</a> to <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> and is based in <a href="/wiki/Wellington" title="Wellington">Wellington</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 2010 constitution gives authority for the islands to operate as a <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a>, with the United Kingdom retaining responsibility for matters such as defence and foreign affairs. The Governor and the Island Council may enact laws for the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peace,_order_and_good_government" title="Peace, order and good government">peace, order and good government</a>" of Pitcairn. The <a href="/wiki/Island_Council_(Pitcairn)" title="Island Council (Pitcairn)">Island Council</a> customarily appoints a <a href="/wiki/List_of_rulers_of_the_Pitcairn_Islands" title="List of rulers of the Pitcairn Islands">Mayor of Pitcairn</a> as a day-to-day head of the local administration. There is a Commissioner, appointed by the Governor, who liaises between the Council and the Governor\'s office.\n</p><p>Since 2015, same-sex marriage has been legal on Pitcairn Island, although there are no people on the island known to be in such a relationship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Pitcairn Islands has the smallest population of any democracy in the world.\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Committee_on_Decolonization" title="United Nations Committee on Decolonization">United Nations Committee on Decolonization</a> includes the Pitcairn Islands on the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_list_of_Non-Self-Governing_Territories" title="United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories">United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Pitcairn Islands are an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_overseas_territories" title="British overseas territories">overseas territory of the United Kingdom</a>; defence is the responsibility of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UK_Ministry_of_Defence" title="UK Ministry of Defence">Ministry of Defence</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Her_Majesty%27s_Armed_Forces" title="Her Majesty\'s Armed Forces">Her Majesty\'s Armed Forces</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-2">[2]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The fertile soil of the Pitcairn valleys, such as Isaac\'s Valley on the gentle slopes southeast of <a href="/wiki/Adamstown,_Pitcairn_Islands" title="Adamstown, Pitcairn Islands">Adamstown</a>, produces a wide variety of fruits: including bananas (Pitkern: <i>plun</i>), <a href="/wiki/Papaya" title="Papaya">papaya</a> (<i>paw paws</i>), <a href="/wiki/Pineapple" title="Pineapple">pineapples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mango" title="Mango">mangoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Watermelon" title="Watermelon">watermelons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cantaloupe" title="Cantaloupe">cantaloupes</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Passionfruit" title="Passionfruit">passionfruit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Breadfruit" title="Breadfruit">breadfruit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">coconuts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avocado" title="Avocado">avocadoes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Citrus" title="Citrus">citrus</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_orange" title="Mandarin orange">mandarin oranges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grapefruit" title="Grapefruit">grapefruit</a>, lemons and <a href="/wiki/Limes" title="Limes">limes</a>). Vegetables include: <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potato" title="Sweet potato">sweet potatoes</a> (kumura), carrots, <a href="/wiki/Sweet_corn" title="Sweet corn">sweet corn</a>, tomatoes, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taro" title="Taro">taro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">yams</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peas" title="Peas">peas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bean" title="Bean">beans</a>. <a href="/wiki/Arrowroot" title="Arrowroot">Arrowroot</a> (<i>Maranta arundinacea</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a> are grown and harvested to produce arrowroot flour and <a href="/wiki/Molasses" title="Molasses">molasses</a>, respectively. Pitcairn Island is remarkably productive and its benign climate supports a wide range of tropical and temperate crops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> All land allocation for any use including agriculture is under the discretion of the government. If the government deems agricultural production excessive then it may tax the land. If the agricultural land has been deemed not up to the standards of the government it may confiscate and transfer the land without compensation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Fish are plentiful in the seas around Pitcairn. <a href="/wiki/Spiny_lobster" title="Spiny lobster">Spiny lobster</a> and a large variety of fish are caught for meals and for trading aboard passing ships. Almost every day someone will go fishing, whether it is from the rocks, from a longboat or diving with a spear gun. There are numerous types of fish around the island. Fish such as nanwee, white fish, moi and opapa are caught in shallow water, while snapper, big eye and cod are caught in deep water, and yellow tail and wahoo are caught by trawling.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minerals">Minerals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Minerals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Manganese, iron, copper, gold, silver and zinc have been discovered within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exclusive_Economic_Zone" title="Exclusive Economic Zone">Exclusive Economic Zone</a>, which extends 370&#160;km (230&#160;mi) offshore and comprises 880,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (340,000&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Honey_production">Honey production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Honey production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1998 the UK\'s overseas aid agency, the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_International_Development" title="Department for International Development">Department for International Development</a>, funded an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apiculture" title="Apiculture">apiculture</a> programme for Pitcairn which included training for Pitcairn\'s <a href="/wiki/Beekeeper" title="Beekeeper">beekeepers</a> and a detailed analysis of Pitcairn\'s bees and honey with particular regard to the presence or absence of disease. Pitcairn has one of the best examples of disease-free bee populations anywhere in the world and the honey produced was and remains exceptionally high in quality. Pitcairn bees are also a placid variety and, within a short time, beekeepers are able to work with them wearing minimal protection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> As a result, Pitcairn exports honey to New Zealand and to the United Kingdom. In London, <a href="/wiki/Fortnum_%26_Mason" title="Fortnum &amp; Mason">Fortnum &amp; Mason</a> sells it and it is a favourite of <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_Charles" title="Prince Charles">Prince Charles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> The Pitcairn Islanders, under the "Bounty Products" and "Delectable Bounty" brands, also export dried fruit including bananas, papayas, pineapples and mangoes to New Zealand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Honey production and all honey related products are a protected monopoly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> All funds and management are under the supervision and discretion of the government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pitcairn.pn_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-pitcairn.pn-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-61">[61]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pepes_ikan_emas_(pais_lauk_mas)_Sunda.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1460" data-file-width="1984" decoding="async" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Pepes_ikan_emas_%28pais_lauk_mas%29_Sunda.jpg/220px-Pepes_ikan_emas_%28pais_lauk_mas%29_Sunda.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Pepes_ikan_emas_%28pais_lauk_mas%29_Sunda.jpg/330px-Pepes_ikan_emas_%28pais_lauk_mas%29_Sunda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Pepes_ikan_emas_%28pais_lauk_mas%29_Sunda.jpg/440px-Pepes_ikan_emas_%28pais_lauk_mas%29_Sunda.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pepes_ikan_emas_(pais_lauk_mas)_Sunda.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Food made from fish and palm leaves</div></div></div>\n<p>Cuisine is not very developed, because only 50 people live on Pitcairn. The most traditional meal is pota, mash from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palm_leaves" title="Palm leaves">palm leaves</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">coconut</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Domestic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_plants" title="Tropical plants">tropical plants</a> are abundantly used. These include: <a href="/wiki/Basil" title="Basil">basil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Breadfruit" title="Breadfruit">breadfruit</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" title="Sugar cane">sugar cane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">coconut</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bananas" title="Bananas">bananas</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beans" title="Beans">beans</a>. <a href="/wiki/Meat" title="Meat">Meat</a> courses consist mainly of <a href="/wiki/Fish_Meat" title="Fish Meat">fish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beef" title="Beef">beef</a>. A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palm_leaf" title="Palm leaf">palm leaf</a> is used in the pictured cuisine. Because most of the population is from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UK" title="UK">UK</a>, the cuisine is influenced by <a href="/wiki/British_cuisine" title="British cuisine">British cuisine</a>, for example, the <a href="/wiki/Meat_pie" title="Meat pie">meat pie</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The cuisine of <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Island" title="Norfolk Island">Norfolk Island</a> is very similar to that of the Pitcairn Islands, as Norfolk Islanders trace their origins to Pitcairn. The local cuisine is a blend of <a href="/wiki/British_cuisine" title="British cuisine">British cuisine</a> and Tahitian cuisine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Recipes from Norfolk Island of Pitcairn origin include mudda (green banana dumplings) and kumara pilhi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The island\'s cuisine also includes foods not found on Pitcairn, such as chopped salads and fruit pies, from the influences of American <a href="/wiki/Whaling" title="Whaling">whalers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Tourism plays a major role on Pitcairn. Tourism is the focus for building the economy. It focuses on small groups coming by charter vessel and staying at "home stays". About ten times a year, passengers from expedition-type cruise ships come ashore for a day, weather permitting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FCO_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-FCO-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Since 2009, the government has been operating the <span class="nowrap"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MV_Claymore_2" title="MV Claymore 2">MV <i>Claymore II</i></a></span> as the island\'s only dedicated passenger/cargo vessel, providing adventure tourism holidays to Pitcairn for <span class="nowrap">three-day or ten-day</span> visits. Tourists stay with local families and experience the island\'s culture while contributing to the local economy. Providing accommodation is a growing source of revenue, and some families have invested in private self-contained units adjacent to their homes for tourists to rent.\n</p><p>Entry requirements for short stays, up to 14 days, which do not require a visa, and for longer stays, that do require prior clearance, are explained in official documents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> All persons under 16 years of age require prior clearance before landing, irrespective of the length of stay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lesser_revenue_sources">Lesser revenue sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Lesser revenue sources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Pitcairners are involved in creating crafts and curios (made out of wood from <a href="/wiki/Henderson_Island_(Pitcairn_Islands)" title="Henderson Island (Pitcairn Islands)">Henderson</a>). Typical woodcarvings include sharks, fish, whales, dolphins, turtles, vases, birds, walking sticks, book boxes, and models of the <i>Bounty</i>. Miro (<i><a href="/wiki/Thespesia_populnea" title="Thespesia populnea">Thespesia populnea</a></i>), a dark and durable wood, is preferred for carving. Islanders also produce <a href="/wiki/Tapa_cloth" title="Tapa cloth">tapa cloth</a> and painted Hattie leaves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The major sources of revenue<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (October 2015)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> have been the sale of coins and postage stamps to collectors, <a href="/wiki/.pn" title=".pn">.pn</a> domain names, and the sale of handicrafts to passing ships, most of which are on the United Kingdom to New Zealand route via the <a href="/wiki/Panama_Canal" title="Panama Canal">Panama Canal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> The flow of funds from these revenue sources are from customer to the government to the Pitcairners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-61">[61]</a></sup> The government holds a monopoly over "any article of whatsoever nature made, manufactured, prepared for sale or produced by any of the inhabitants of Pitcairn Island".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pitcairn.pn_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-pitcairn.pn-60">[60]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electricity">Electricity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Electricity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Diesel generators provide the island with electricity from 7&#160;am to 10&#160;pm. A wind power plant was planned to be installed to help reduce the high cost of power generation associated with the import of diesel, but was cancelled in 2013 after a project overrun of three years and a cost of &#163;250,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The only qualified high voltage electricity technician on Pitcairn, who manages the electricity grid, reached the age of 65 in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-government.pn_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-government.pn-13">[13]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Pitcairn_Islanders" title="Pitcairn Islanders">Pitcairn Islanders</a> and <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Pitcairn_Islands" title="Demographics of the Pitcairn Islands">Demographics of the Pitcairn Islands</a></div>\n<p>The islands have suffered a substantial population decline since 1940, and the viability of the island\'s community is in doubt (see <a href="#Potential_extinction">&#167;&#160;Potential extinction</a>, below). The government has tried to attract migrants. However, these initiatives have not been effective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-star_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-star-77">[77]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Only two children were born on Pitcairn in the 21 years prior to 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> In 2005, Shirley and Simon Young became the first married outsider couple in history to obtain citizenship on Pitcairn.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_Pitcairn_Islands" title="Languages of the Pitcairn Islands">Languages of the Pitcairn Islands</a></div>\n<p>Most resident Pitcairn Islanders are <a href="/wiki/Descendants_of_the_Bounty_mutineers" title="Descendants of the Bounty mutineers">descendants of the <i>Bounty</i> mutineers</a> and Tahitians (or other Polynesians). <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitkern" title="Pitkern">Pitkern</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">creole language</a> derived from 18th-century English, with elements of the <a href="/wiki/Tahitian_language" title="Tahitian language">Tahitian language</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-39">[39]</a></sup> It is spoken as a first language by the population and is taught alongside English at the island\'s only school. It is closely related to the creole language <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norfuk" title="Norfuk">Norfuk</a>, spoken on <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Island" title="Norfolk Island">Norfolk Island</a>, because Norfolk was repopulated in the mid-19th century by Pitcairners.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The only church building on the island is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist" title="Seventh-day Adventist">Seventh-day Adventist</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_2-5"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-2">[2]</a></sup> The Seventh-Day Adventist Church is not a <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a>, as no laws concerning its establishment were passed by the local government. A successful Seventh-day Adventist mission in the 1890s was important in shaping Pitcairn society. In recent years, the church population has declined, and as of  2000<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, eight of the then forty islanders attended services regularly,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ANN_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-ANN-80">[80]</a></sup> but most attend church on special occasions. From Friday at sunset until Saturday at sunset, Pitcairners observe a day of rest in observance of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sabbath_and_Seventh-day_Adventism" title="Sabbath and Seventh-day Adventism">Sabbath</a>, or as a mark of respect for observant Adventists.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pitcairn_-_Church_of_Adamstown.jpg"><img alt="Adamstown" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1026" data-file-width="1496" decoding="async" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Pitcairn_-_Church_of_Adamstown.jpg/220px-Pitcairn_-_Church_of_Adamstown.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Pitcairn_-_Church_of_Adamstown.jpg/330px-Pitcairn_-_Church_of_Adamstown.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Pitcairn_-_Church_of_Adamstown.jpg/440px-Pitcairn_-_Church_of_Adamstown.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pitcairn_-_Church_of_Adamstown.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Church of Adamstown</div></div></div>\n<p>The church was built in 1954 and is run by the Church board and resident pastor, who usually serves a two-year term. The Sabbath School meets at 10&#160;am on Saturday mornings, and is followed by Divine Service an hour later. On Tuesday evenings, there is another service in the form of a prayer meeting.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Education is free and compulsory between the ages of five and sixteen. Children up to the age of 12 are taught at Pulau School, while children of 13 and over attend secondary school in New Zealand, or are educated via correspondence school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The island\'s children have produced a book in Pitkern and English called <i>Mi Bas Side orn Pitcairn</i> or <i>My Favourite Place on Pitcairn</i>.\n</p><p>The school at Pitcairn, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pulau_School&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pulau School (page does not exist)">Pulau School</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;[<a class="extiw" href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pulau_School" title="de:Pulau School">de</a>]</span>, provides pre-school and primary education based on the New Zealand syllabus. The teacher is appointed by the governor from suitable qualified applicants who are registered teachers.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_population">Historical population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Historical population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Pitcairn\'s population has significantly decreased since its peak of over 200 in the 1930s, to only around fifty permanent residents today (2012&#8211;2018).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:right">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Year</th>\n<th>Population</th>\n<th>Year</th>\n<th>Population</th>\n<th>Year</th>\n<th>Population</th>\n<th>Year</th>\n<th>Population</th>\n<th>Year</th>\n<th>Population</th>\n<th>Year</th>\n<th>Population\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1790</td>\n<td>27</td>\n<td>1880</td>\n<td>112</td>\n<td>1970</td>\n<td>96</td>\n<td>1992</td>\n<td>54</td>\n<td>2002</td>\n<td>48</td>\n<td>2012</td>\n<td>48\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1800</td>\n<td>34</td>\n<td>1890</td>\n<td>136</td>\n<td>1975</td>\n<td>74</td>\n<td>1993</td>\n<td>57</td>\n<td>2003</td>\n<td>59</td>\n<td>2013</td>\n<td>56\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1810</td>\n<td>50</td>\n<td>1900</td>\n<td>136</td>\n<td>1980</td>\n<td>61</td>\n<td>1994</td>\n<td>54</td>\n<td>2004</td>\n<td>65</td>\n<td>2014</td>\n<td>56\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1820</td>\n<td>66</td>\n<td>1910</td>\n<td>140</td>\n<td>1985</td>\n<td>58</td>\n<td>1995</td>\n<td>55</td>\n<td>2005</td>\n<td>63</td>\n<td>2015</td>\n<td>50\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1830</td>\n<td>70</td>\n<td>1920</td>\n<td>163</td>\n<td>1986</td>\n<td>68</td>\n<td>1996</td>\n<td>43</td>\n<td>2006</td>\n<td>65</td>\n<td>2016</td>\n<td>49\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1840</td>\n<td>119</td>\n<td>1930</td>\n<td>190</td>\n<td>1987</td>\n<td>59</td>\n<td>1997</td>\n<td>40</td>\n<td>2007</td>\n<td>64</td>\n<td>2017</td>\n<td>50\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1850</td>\n<td>146</td>\n<td>1936</td>\n<td>250</td>\n<td>1988</td>\n<td>55</td>\n<td>1998</td>\n<td>66</td>\n<td>2008</td>\n<td>66</td>\n<td>2018</td>\n<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[i]</a></sup>50\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1856</td>\n<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[ii]</a></sup>193</td>\n<td>1940</td>\n<td>163</td>\n<td>1989</td>\n<td>55</td>\n<td>1999</td>\n<td>46</td>\n<td>2009</td>\n<td>67</td>\n<td></td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1859</td>\n<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[iii]</a></sup>16</td>\n<td>1950</td>\n<td>161</td>\n<td>1990</td>\n<td>59</td>\n<td>2000</td>\n<td>51</td>\n<td>2010</td>\n<td>64</td>\n<td></td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1870</td>\n<td>70</td>\n<td>1960</td>\n<td>126</td>\n<td>1991</td>\n<td>66</td>\n<td>2001</td>\n<td>44</td>\n<td>2011</td>\n<td>67</td>\n<td></td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-roman;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-84"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-84">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Latest population figure<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-visitpitcairn.pn_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-visitpitcairn.pn-3">[3]</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-85"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-85">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Migration to Norfolk Island in 1856 left Pitcairn uninhabited</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-86"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-86">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">First group returns from Norfolk Island</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Potential_extinction">Potential extinction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Potential extinction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As of  July&#160;2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the total resident population of the Pitcairn Islands was 56, including the six temporary residents: an administrator, a doctor, a police officer, and their spouses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-population-87">[84]</a></sup> However, the actual permanent resident population was only 49&#160;Pitcairners spread across 23&#160;households.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-government.pn_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-government.pn-13">[13]</a></sup> It is, however, rare for all 49 residents to be on-island at the same time; it is common for several residents to be off-island for varying lengths of time visiting family, for medical reasons, or to attend international conferences. As of  November&#160;2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> for instance, seven residents were off-island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-government.pn_13-3"><a href="#cite_note-government.pn-13">[13]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Diaspora" title="Diaspora">diaspora</a> survey projected that by 2045, if nothing were done, only three people of working age would be left on the island, with the rest being very old. In addition, the survey revealed that residents who had left the island over the past decades showed little interest in coming back. Of the hundreds of emigrants contacted, only 33 were willing to participate in the survey and just three expressed a desire to return.\n</p><p>As of  2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the labour force consisted of 31&#160;able-bodied persons: 17&#160;males and 14&#160;females between 18 and 64&#160;years of age. Of the 31, just seven are younger than 40, but 18 are over the age of 50.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-government.pn_13-4"><a href="#cite_note-government.pn-13">[13]</a></sup> Most of the men undertake the more strenuous physical tasks on the island such as crewing the longboats, cargo handling, and the operation and maintenance of physical assets. Longboat crew retirement age is 58. There were then 12&#160;men aged between 18 and 58 residing on Pitcairn. Each longboat requires a minimum crew of three; of the four longboat <a href="/wiki/Coxswain" title="Coxswain">coxswains</a>, two were in their late 50s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-government.pn_13-5"><a href="#cite_note-government.pn-13">[13]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Pitcairn government\'s attempts to attract migrants have been unsuccessful. Since 2013, some 700 make inquiries each year, but so far, not a single formal settlement application has been received.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-government.pn_13-6"><a href="#cite_note-government.pn-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-star_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-star-77">[77]</a></sup> The migrants are prohibited from taking local jobs or claiming benefits for a certain length of time, even those with children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[85]</a></sup> The migrants are expected to have at least NZ$&#8239;30&#8239;000 per person in savings and are expected to build their own house at average cost of NZ$&#8239;140&#8239;000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billhaigh_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-billhaigh-89">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Menzies_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Menzies-90">[87]</a></sup> It is also possible to bring off-island builders at an additional cost of between NZ$&#8239;23&#8239;000 and NZ$&#8239;28&#8239;000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Menzies_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-Menzies-90">[87]</a></sup> The average annual cost of living on the island is NZ$&#8239;9464.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billhaigh_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-billhaigh-89">[86]</a></sup> There is, however, no assurance of the migrant\'s right to remain on Pitcairn; after their first two years, the council must review and reapprove the migrant\'s status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[88]</a></sup> The migrants are also required to take part in the unpaid public work to keep the island in order: maintain the island\'s numerous roads and paths, build roads, navigate the island longboats, clean public toilets, etc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[89]</a></sup> There are also restrictions on bringing children under the age of 16 to the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gay_2013_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gay_2013-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.gov.uk_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-www.gov.uk-93">[90]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Freight from <a href="/wiki/Tauranga" title="Tauranga">Tauranga</a> to Pitcairn on the <span class="nowrap">MV <i>Claymore II</i></span> (Pitcairn Island\'s dedicated passenger and cargo ship chartered by the Pitcairn government) is charged at NZ$&#8239;350/m&#179; for Pitcairners and NZ$&#8239;1000/m&#179; for all other freight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[91]</a></sup> Additionally, Pitcairners are charged NZ$&#8239;3000 for a one-way trip; others are charged NZ$&#8239;5000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-government.pn_13-7"><a href="#cite_note-government.pn-13">[13]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the government\'s Pitcairn Islands Economic Report stated that "[no one] will migrate to Pitcairn Islands for economic reasons as there are limited government jobs, a lack of private sector employment, as well as considerable competition for the tourism dollar". The Pitcairners take tourists in turns to accommodate those few tourists who occasionally visit the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-government.pn_13-8"><a href="#cite_note-government.pn-13">[13]</a></sup>\n</p><p>As the island remains a British Overseas Territory, at some point the British government may have to make a decision about the island\'s future.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[93]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_the_Pitcairn_Islands_and_Norfolk_Island" title="Cuisine of the Pitcairn Islands and Norfolk Island">Cuisine of the Pitcairn Islands and Norfolk Island</a></div>\n<p>The once-strict moral codes, which prohibited dancing, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_displays_of_affection" title="Public displays of affection">public displays of affection</a>, smoking, and consumption of alcohol, have been relaxed. Islanders and visitors no longer require a six-month licence to purchase, import, and consume alcohol.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[94]</a></sup> There is now one licensed caf&#233; and bar on the island, and the government store sells alcohol and cigarettes.\n</p><p>Fishing and swimming are two popular recreational activities. A birthday celebration or the arrival of a ship or yacht will involve the entire Pitcairn community in a public dinner in the Square, Adamstown. Tables are covered in a variety of foods, including fish, meat, chicken, pilhi, baked rice, boiled <i>plun</i> (banana), breadfruit, vegetable dishes, an assortment of pies, bread, breadsticks, an array of desserts, pineapple and watermelon.\n</p><p>Paid employees maintain the island\'s numerous roads and paths. As of  2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the island had a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labour_force" title="Labour force">labour force</a> of over 35 men and women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_2-6"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-2">[2]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bounty_Day" title="Bounty Day">Bounty Day</a> is an annual <a href="/wiki/Public_holiday" title="Public holiday">public holiday</a> celebrated on Pitcairn on 23 January<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[95]</a></sup> to commemorate the day in 1790 when the mutineers arrived on the island in HMS <i>Bounty</i>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_communications">Media and communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Media and communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<dl><dt>Mail</dt>\n<dd>The <a href="/wiki/Postcodes_in_the_United_Kingdom#British_Overseas_Territories" title="Postcodes in the United Kingdom">UK Postcode</a> for directing mail to Pitcairn Island is PCRN 1ZZ.</dd>\n<dt>Telephones</dt>\n<dd></dd></dl>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbers_in_the_Pitcairn_Islands" title="Telephone numbers in the Pitcairn Islands">Telephone numbers in the Pitcairn Islands</a></div>\n<p>Pitcairn uses New Zealand\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_country_calling_codes" title="List of country calling codes">international calling code</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%2B64" title="+64">+64</a>. It is still on the <a href="/wiki/Telephone_exchange#Manual_service_exchanges" title="Telephone exchange">manual telephone system</a>.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Radio</dt>\n<dd>There is no broadcast station. Marine band <a href="/wiki/Walkie-talkie" title="Walkie-talkie">walkie-talkie</a> radios are used to maintain contact among people in different areas of the island. Foreign stations can be picked up on <a href="/wiki/Shortwave_radio" title="Shortwave radio">shortwave radio</a>.</dd>\n<dt>Amateur radio</dt>\n<dd>Callsign website <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/QRZ.COM" title="QRZ.COM">QRZ.COM</a> lists six <a href="/wiki/Amateur_radio" title="Amateur radio">amateur radio</a> operators on the island, using the <a href="/wiki/ITU_prefix" title="ITU prefix">ITU prefix</a> (assigned through the UK) of VP6. However, some of those operators have died, while others are no longer active. The last <a href="/wiki/DX-pedition" title="DX-pedition">DX-pedition</a> to Pitcairn took place in 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[96]</a></sup> In 2008, a major DX-pedition visited <a href="/wiki/Ducie_Island" title="Ducie Island">Ducie Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[97]</a></sup>  In 2018, another major DX-pedition visited <a href="/wiki/Ducie_Island" title="Ducie Island">Ducie Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[98]</a></sup></dd>\n<dt>Television</dt>\n<dd>Pitcairn can receive a number of television channels but only has capacity to broadcast two channels to houses at any one time. The channels are currently switched on a regular basis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[99]</a></sup></dd>\n<dt>Internet</dt>\n<dd>There is one government-sponsored <a href="/wiki/Satellite_Internet_access" title="Satellite Internet access">satellite internet</a> connection, with networking provided to the inhabitants of the island. Pitcairn\'s <a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">country code top-level domain</a> is <a href="/wiki/.pn" title=".pn">.pn</a>. Residents pay NZ$&#8239;100 (about &#163;50) for 2<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Gigabyte" title="Gigabyte">GB</a> of data per month, at a rate of 256<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kbit/s" title="Kbit/s">kbit/s</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[100]</a></sup> In 2012, a single 1Mbit/s link installed provided the islanders with an internet connection, the 1Mbit/s was shared across all families on the island. By December 2017, the British Government implemented a 4G LTE mobile network in Adamstown with shared speeds of 5 Mbit/s across all islanders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[101]</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>All settlers of the Pitcairn Islands arrived by boat or ship. Pitcairn Island does not have an airport, airstrip or seaport; the islanders rely on <a href="/wiki/Longboat" title="Longboat">longboats</a> to ferry people and goods between visiting ships and shore through Bounty Bay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FCO_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-FCO-69">[69]</a></sup> Access to the rest of the shoreline is restricted by jagged rocks. The island has one shallow harbour with a launch ramp accessible only by small <a href="/wiki/Surfboat" title="Surfboat">longboats</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[102]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A dedicated passenger and cargo supply ship chartered by the Pitcairn Island government, the <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/MV_Claymore_II" title="MV Claymore II">MV <i>Claymore II</i></a></span>, is the principal transport from <a href="/wiki/Mangareva" title="Mangareva">Mangareva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gambier_Islands" title="Gambier Islands">Gambier Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_Polynesia" title="French Polynesia">French Polynesia</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Totegegie_Airport" title="Totegegie Airport">Totegegie Airport</a> in Mangareva can be reached by air from the French Polynesian capital <a href="/wiki/Papeete" title="Papeete">Papeete</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[103]</a></sup>\n</p><p>There is one 6.4-kilometre (4&#160;mi) paved road leading up from Bounty Bay through Adamstown.\n</p><p>The main modes of transport on Pitcairn Islands are by four-wheel drive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quad_bike" title="Quad bike">quad bikes</a> and on foot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FCO_69-2"><a href="#cite_note-FCO-69">[69]</a></sup> Much of the road and track network and some of the footpaths of Pitcairn Island are viewable on <a href="/wiki/Google_Street_View" title="Google Street View">Google\'s Street View</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[105]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ned_Young" title="Ned Young">Ned Young</a> (c.1762&#8211;1800 in Pitcairn) mutineer from the famous HMS Bounty incident, and co-founder of the mutineers\' Pitcairn Island settlement.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/William_McCoy_(mutineer)" title="William McCoy (mutineer)">William McCoy</a> (c.1763&#8211;1798 in Pitcairn) a Scottish sailor and a mutineer on board HMS Bounty.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fletcher_Christian" title="Fletcher Christian">Fletcher Christian</a> (1764 &#8211; 1793 in Pitcairn) Master\'s mate on board HMS <i>Bounty</i>, died here at age 28.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kirk_2012_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kirk_2012-109">[106]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Matthew_Quintal" title="Matthew Quintal">Matthew Quintal</a> (1766&#8211;1799 in Pitcairn) was a Cornish able seaman and mutineer aboard HMS Bounty</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/John_Adams_(mutineer)" title="John Adams (mutineer)">John Adams</a> (1767&#8211;1829 in Pitcairn) the last survivor of the HMS Bounty mutineers who settled on Pitcairn Island in January 1790, the year after the mutiny</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Thursday_October_Christian_I" title="Thursday October Christian I">Thursday October Christian I</a> (1790 &#8211; 1831) was the first son of <a href="/wiki/Fletcher_Christian" title="Fletcher Christian">Fletcher Christian</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/George_Adams_(magistrate)" title="George Adams (magistrate)">George Adams</a> (1804&#8211;1873) served as Chief Magistrate on Pitcairn in 1848</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Thursday_October_Christian_II" title="Thursday October Christian II">Thursday October Christian II</a> (1820 &#8211; 1911) was a Pitcairn Islands political leader. Grandson of <a href="/wiki/Fletcher_Christian" title="Fletcher Christian">Fletcher Christian</a> and son of <a href="/wiki/Thursday_October_Christian_I" title="Thursday October Christian I">Thursday October Christian I</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Simon_Young_(magistrate)" title="Simon Young (magistrate)">Simon Young</a> (1823-1893) served as Magistrate of the Pitcairn Islands in 1849</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Moses_Young" title="Moses Young">Moses Young</a> (1829&#8211;1909) served as magistrate of Pitcairn Island four times, between 1865 and 1881</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/James_Russell_McCoy" title="James Russell McCoy">James Russell McCoy</a> (1845 &#8211; 1924) served as Magistrate of Pitcairn Island 7 times, between 1870 and 1904</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Stanley_Young" title="Benjamin Stanley Young">Benjamin Stanley Young</a> (1851&#8211;1934) served as Magistrate of the Pitcairn Islands twice, from 1884 to 1885, and in 1892</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rosalind_Amelia_Young" title="Rosalind Amelia Young">Rosalind Amelia Young</a> (1853&#8211;1924) a historian from Pitcairn Islands</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/William_Alfred_Young" title="William Alfred Young">William Alfred Young</a> (1863&#8211;1911) served as President of the Council, and Magistrate of Pitcairn Island three times, between 1897 and 1908</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Matthew_Edmond_McCoy" title="Matthew Edmond McCoy">Matthew Edmond McCoy</a> (1868 - 1929) served as Magistrate of Pitcairn Island in 1909</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gerard_Bromley_Robert_Christian" title="Gerard Bromley Robert Christian">Gerard Bromley Robert Christian</a> (1870 - 1919) served as Magistrate of Pitcairn Island from 1910 to 1919</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Edgar_Allen_Christian" title="Edgar Allen Christian">Edgar Allen Christian</a> (1879 &#8211; 1960) politician from Pitcairn and Chief Magistrate of Pitcairn Island on several occasions between 1923 and 1939</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Charles_Richard_Parkin_Christian" title="Charles Richard Parkin Christian">Charles Richard Parkin Christian</a> (1883 - 1971) a long-serving politician from Pitcairn and Chief Magistrate of Pitcairn Island for eleven years at various times between 1920 and 1957</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Martin_Christian" title="Frederick Martin Christian">Frederick Martin Christian</a> (1883 &#8211; 1971) a politician from Pitcairn and Chief Magistrate of Pitcairn Island on three occasions between 1921 and 1943</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/John_Lorenzo_Christian" title="John Lorenzo Christian">John Lorenzo Christian</a> (1895 - 1984) served as Chief Magistrate of Pitcairn Island, twice in 1952-54 and 1961&#8211;66</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ivan_Christian" title="Ivan Christian">Ivan Christian</a> (1919 &#8211; 1991) politician from Pitcairn and Chief Magistrate of Pitcairn Island from 1976 to 1984</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Brenda_Christian" title="Brenda Christian">Brenda Christian</a> (born 1953) political figure from the Pitcairn Islands and served the territory as its first female Mayor from 8 November to 15 December 2004</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tom_Christian" title="Tom Christian">Tom Christian</a> (1935 - 2013) radio operator</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" Island\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pitcairn_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul
